%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Inverter voltage utilization for naive three-phase PWM %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Inverter voltage utilization for naive three-phase PWM}
    Assume linear modulation for all three phases, i.e.,
    $$s_\mathrm{a}^*(t) = m^* \sin\left(\omega t\right), \quad s_\mathrm{b}^*(t) = m^* \sin\left(\omega t - \frac{2\pi}{3}\right), \quad s_\mathrm{c}^*(t) = m^* \sin\left(\omega t - \frac{4\pi}{3}\right), \quad \text{with} \quad m^*\leq1 .$$ Hence, we have
    \begin{equation}
        \left\{|s^*_\mathrm{a}|, |s^*_\mathrm{b}|, |s^*_\mathrm{c}|\right\} \leq 1.
        \label{eq:linear_mod_per_phase_max}
    \end{equation}
    From \eqref{eq:Clarke_transformation_zero_component_free_inverse} we can relate the reference normalized phase voltages to the $\upalpha\upbeta$-plane as:
    \begin{equation}
        s^*_\mathrm{a} = s^*_\upalpha, \quad s^*_\mathrm{b} = -\frac{1}{2}s^*_\upalpha + \frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}s^*_\upbeta, \quad s^*_\mathrm{c} = -\frac{1}{2}s^*_\upalpha - \frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}s^*_\upbeta.
        \label{eq:average_switching_values_abc_alpha_beta}
    \end{equation}
    Combining \eqref{eq:linear_mod_per_phase_max} and \eqref{eq:average_switching_values_abc_alpha_beta} yields the maximum achievable $\upalpha\upbeta$-reference voltage magnitude for the naive three-phase PWM (cf. \figref{fig:naive_three_phase_pwm_alpha_beta_voltage_limit}):
    \begin{equation}
        \left|s^*_\upalpha\vphantom{-\frac{1}{2}s^*_\upalpha + \frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}s^*_\upbeta}\right|\leq 1, \quad \left|-\frac{1}{2}s^*_\upalpha + \frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}s^*_\upbeta\right| \leq 1, \quad \left|-\frac{1}{2}s^*_\upalpha - \frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}s^*_\upbeta\right| \leq 1.
        \label{eq:maximum_achievable_alpha_beta_voltage}
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Inverter voltage utilization for naive three-phase PWM (cont.) %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}[b]
    \frametitle{Inverter voltage utilization for naive three-phase PWM (cont.)}
    \begin{columns}[onlytextwidth]
        \begin{column}{0.47\textwidth}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item The three independent single-phase PWMs underutilize the available voltage range of the three-phase inverter.
                \item The maximum achievable fundamental normalized voltage reference is $$|\bm{s}_{\upalpha\upbeta}| \leq 1,$$ that is, $$|\bm{u}^*_{\upalpha\upbeta}| \leq \nicefrac{u_\mathrm{dc}}{2}.$$
                \item Naively extending the voltage range by overmodulating each phase is theoretically possible but leads to significant harmonic distortion. Hence, we explore an alternative approach next.
            \end{itemize}
        \end{column}
        \begin{column}{0.47\textwidth}
            \centering
            \vspace{-0.25cm}
            \begin{figure}
                \begin{tikzpicture}[x=1.25cm,y=1.25cm,>=Latex]
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\outerRadius}{2}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\innerRadius}{sqrt(3)}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\linearRadius}{1.5}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\axisExtension}{1.1*\outerRadius}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\tickHalf}{0.08}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\alphaLeaderShiftX}{0.03}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\alphaLeaderShiftY}{-0.15}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\alphaLeaderDx}{0.10}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\alphaLeaderDy}{-0.28}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\betaLeaderShiftX}{0.08}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\betaLeaderShiftY}{0.08}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\betaLeaderDx}{0.35}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\betaLeaderDy}{0.20}

                    \coordinate (origin) at (0,0);
                    \foreach \name/\angle in {u1/0,u2/60,u3/120,u4/180,u5/240,u6/300} {
                            \coordinate (\name) at (\angle:\outerRadius);
                        }
                    \foreach \name/\angle in {m1/30,m2/90,m3/150,m4/210,m5/270,m6/330} {
                            \coordinate (\name) at (\angle:\innerRadius);
                        }
                    \coordinate (circleRadius) at (30:\linearRadius);
                    \coordinate (betaMax) at (90:\innerRadius);
                    \coordinate (alphaAxisStart) at (180:\axisExtension);
                    \coordinate (alphaAxisEnd) at (0:\axisExtension);
                    \coordinate (betaAxisStart) at (270:\axisExtension);
                    \coordinate (betaAxisEnd) at (90:\axisExtension);
                    \coordinate (bAxisStart) at (300:\axisExtension);
                    \coordinate (bAxisEnd) at (120:\axisExtension);
                    \coordinate (cAxisStart) at (60:\axisExtension);
                    \coordinate (cAxisEnd) at (240:\axisExtension);

                    \begin{scope}[on background layer]
                        \fill[signalalpha!15] (m1) -- (m2) -- (m3) -- (m4) -- (m5) -- (m6) -- cycle;
                    \end{scope}
                    \draw[->,thin] (alphaAxisStart) -- (alphaAxisEnd) node[right] {$s^*_{\upalpha}, s^*_{\mathrm{a}}$};
                    \draw[->,thin] (betaAxisStart) -- (betaAxisEnd) node[left] {$s^*_{\upbeta}$};
                    \draw[->,thin] (bAxisStart) -- (bAxisEnd) node[above left] {$s^*_{\mathrm{b}}$};
                    \draw[->,thin] (cAxisStart) -- (cAxisEnd) node[below left] {$s^*_{\mathrm{c}}$};
                    \draw[gray!70,thick] (u1) -- (u2) -- (u3) -- (u4) -- (u5) -- (u6) -- cycle;
                    \draw[signalalpha!65,thick] (m1) -- (m2) -- (m3) -- (m4) -- (m5) -- (m6) -- cycle;
                    \draw[signalalpha,thick] (origin) circle[radius=\linearRadius];
                    \draw[signalalpha,->,thick] (origin) -- (circleRadius) node[near end, below] {$1$};

                    \draw[thin] (u1) ++(0,\tickHalf) -- ++(0,-2*\tickHalf);
                    \draw[thin] ($(u1) + (\alphaLeaderShiftX,\alphaLeaderShiftY)$) -- ++(\alphaLeaderDx,\alphaLeaderDy) node[below right] {$\frac{4}{3}$};

                    \draw[thin] (betaMax) ++(\betaLeaderShiftX,\betaLeaderShiftY) -- ++(\betaLeaderDx,\betaLeaderDy) node[above right] {$\frac{2}{\sqrt{3}}$};
                    \draw[thin] (betaMax) ++(\betaLeaderShiftX,0) -- ++(-2*\betaLeaderShiftX,0);
                \end{tikzpicture}


                \caption{Maximum achievable $\upalpha\upbeta$-reference voltage for the naive three-phase PWM}
                \label{fig:naive_three_phase_pwm_alpha_beta_voltage_limit}
            \end{figure}
        \end{column}
    \end{columns}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\subsection{Three-phase zero-sequence injection}
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Three-phase PWM with zero-sequence injection %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Three-phase PWM with zero-sequence injection}
    Subtract a zero-sequence component from all phase references
    \begin{equation}
        u_\mathrm{a}^{**}(t) = u_\mathrm{a}^*(t) - u_0(t), \quad u_\mathrm{b}^{**}(t) = u_\mathrm{b}^*(t) - u_0(t), \quad u_\mathrm{c}^{**}(t) = u_\mathrm{c}^*(t) - u_0(t)
    \end{equation}
    does not change the line-to-line voltages
    \begin{equation}
        u_\mathrm{a\text{-}b}^{**}(t) = u_\mathrm{a}^{**}(t) - u_\mathrm{b}^{**}(t) = u_\mathrm{a}^*(t) - u_\mathrm{b}^*(t) = u_\mathrm{a\text{-}b}^*(t), \quad \text{etc.}
    \end{equation}
    and hence does not change the $\upalpha\upbeta$-reference voltage, compare \eqref{eq:Clarke_transformation_zero_component_free}. Consequently, the \hl{zero-sequence injection is not a disturbance from a control perspective}. To find $u_0$, we formulate the following optimization problem (dropping the time argument for better readability):
    \begin{equation}
        \min_{u_0} \max \left\{|u^*_\mathrm{a}-u_0|, |u^*_\mathrm{b}-u_0|, |u^*_\mathrm{c}-u_0|\right\},
        \label{eq:opt_problem_zero_sequence_PWM}
    \end{equation}
    i.e., we want to \hl{find the smallest possible zero-sequence component that is required to meet the highest phase voltage demand}.
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Three-phase PWM with zero-sequence injection (cont.)%%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Three-phase PWM with zero-sequence injection (cont.)}
    The problem \eqref{eq:opt_problem_zero_sequence_PWM} is equivalent to
    \begin{equation}
        \min_{u_0, r} r \quad \text{subject to} \quad |u^*_\mathrm{a}-u_0| \leq r, \; |u^*_\mathrm{b}-u_0| \leq r, \; |u^*_\mathrm{c}-u_0| \leq r
    \end{equation}
    with $r\in\mathbb{R}\geq 0$ representing the maximum deviation of the zero-sequence injected phase voltages from the original reference voltages. Rewriting the constraints yields
    \begin{equation}
        u_\mathrm{a}^* - r \leq u_0 \leq u_\mathrm{a}^* + r, \quad u_\mathrm{b}^* - r \leq u_0 \leq u_\mathrm{b}^* + r, \quad u_\mathrm{c}^* - r \leq u_0 \leq u_\mathrm{c}^* + r.
    \end{equation}
    Hence, a feasible $u_0$ exists if and if only the three intervals overlap, i.e.,
    \begin{equation}
        \max\left\{u^*_\mathrm{a}-r, u^*_\mathrm{b}-r, u^*_\mathrm{c}-r\right\} \leq \min\left\{u^*_\mathrm{a}+r, u^*_\mathrm{b}+r, u^*_\mathrm{c}+r\right\}.
        \label{eq:feasible_intervals_r_zero_volt_inject}
    \end{equation}
    Define the auxiliary variables
    \begin{equation}
        u_\mathrm{max} = \max\left\{u^*_\mathrm{a}, u^*_\mathrm{b}, u^*_\mathrm{c}\right\}, \quad u_\mathrm{min} = \min\left\{u^*_\mathrm{a}, u^*_\mathrm{b}, u^*_\mathrm{c}\right\}.
        \label{eq:aux_variables_zero_volt_inject}
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Three-phase PWM with zero-sequence injection (cont.)%%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Three-phase PWM with zero-sequence injection (cont.)}
    Combining \eqref{eq:feasible_intervals_r_zero_volt_inject} and \eqref{eq:aux_variables_zero_volt_inject} yields
    \begin{equation}
        u_\mathrm{max} - r \leq u_\mathrm{min} + r \quad \Leftrightarrow \quad r \geq \frac{u_\mathrm{max} - u_\mathrm{min}}{2}.
        \label{eq:zero_volt_inject_r_max_min_range}
    \end{equation}
    Since we search for the smallest possible $r$, we have
    \begin{equation}
        r = \frac{u_\mathrm{max} - u_\mathrm{min}}{2}.
    \end{equation}
    This observation is identical that the optimal solution is given with equality in \eqref{eq:zero_volt_inject_r_max_min_range}, i.e.,
    \begin{equation}
        u_\mathrm{max} - r = u_\mathrm{min} + r \quad \Leftrightarrow \quad u_0 = \frac{u_\mathrm{max} + u_\mathrm{min}}{2}.
    \end{equation}
    Hence, the \hl{optimal zero-sequence component} is:
    \begin{equation}
        u_0(t) = \frac{1}{2}\left(\max\left\{u^*_\mathrm{a}(t), u^*_\mathrm{b}(t), u^*_\mathrm{c}(t)\right\} + \min\left\{u^*_\mathrm{a}(t), u^*_\mathrm{b}(t), u^*_\mathrm{c}(t)\right\}\right).
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Inverter voltage utilization with zero-sequence injection three-phase PWM %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}[b]
    \frametitle{Inverter voltage utilization with zero-sequence injection three-phase PWM}
    \begin{columns}[onlytextwidth]
        \begin{column}{0.47\textwidth}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item Extends the fundamental voltage range to $$|\bm{s}_{\upalpha\upbeta}| \leq \frac{2}{\sqrt{3}} \approx 1.15.$$
                \item Also allows reaching the entire voltage hexagon incl. the corners (cf. figure to the right and proof in the next slides).
                \item Alternatively a \hl{third harmonic voltage injection} is often used in practice, i.e., $$u_0(t) = \hat{u}_0 \sin\left(3\omega t\right).$$ This approach also increases the modulation range to $\nicefrac{2}{\sqrt{3}}$ but does not allow reaching the hexagon's corners.
            \end{itemize}
        \end{column}
        \begin{column}{0.47\textwidth}
            \centering
            \vspace{-0.25cm}
            \begin{figure}
                \begin{tikzpicture}[x=1.25cm,y=1.25cm,>=Latex]
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\outerRadius}{2}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\innerRadius}{sqrt(3)}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\linearRadius}{\innerRadius}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\axisExtension}{1.1*\outerRadius}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\tickHalf}{0.08}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\alphaLeaderShiftX}{0.03}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\alphaLeaderShiftY}{-0.15}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\alphaLeaderDx}{0.10}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\alphaLeaderDy}{-0.28}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\betaLeaderShiftX}{0.08}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\betaLeaderShiftY}{0.08}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\betaLeaderDx}{0.35}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\betaLeaderDy}{0.20}

                    \coordinate (origin) at (0,0);
                    \foreach \name/\angle in {u1/0,u2/60,u3/120,u4/180,u5/240,u6/300} {
                            \coordinate (\name) at (\angle:\outerRadius);
                        }
                    \foreach \name/\angle in {m1/30,m2/90,m3/150,m4/210,m5/270,m6/330} {
                            \coordinate (\name) at (\angle:\innerRadius);
                        }
                    \coordinate (circleRadius) at (45:\linearRadius);
                    \coordinate (betaMax) at (90:\innerRadius);
                    \coordinate (alphaAxisStart) at (180:\axisExtension);
                    \coordinate (alphaAxisEnd) at (0:\axisExtension);
                    \coordinate (betaAxisStart) at (270:\axisExtension);
                    \coordinate (betaAxisEnd) at (90:\axisExtension);
                    \begin{scope}[on background layer]
                        \fill[signalalpha!15] (u1) -- (u2) -- (u3) -- (u4) -- (u5) -- (u6) -- cycle;
                    \end{scope}
                    \draw[->,thin] (alphaAxisStart) -- (alphaAxisEnd) node[right] {$s^*_{\upalpha}$};
                    \draw[->,thin] (betaAxisStart) -- (betaAxisEnd) node[left] {$s^*_{\upbeta}$};
                    \draw[gray!70,thick] (u1) -- (u2) -- (u3) -- (u4) -- (u5) -- (u6) -- cycle;
                    \draw[signalalpha!65,thick] (u1) -- (u2) -- (u3) -- (u4) -- (u5) -- (u6) -- cycle;
                    \draw[signalalpha,thick] (origin) circle[radius=\linearRadius];
                    \draw[signalalpha,->,thick] (origin) -- (circleRadius) node[near end, below] {$\frac{2}{\sqrt{3}}$};

                    \draw[thin] (u1) ++(0,\tickHalf) -- ++(0,-2*\tickHalf);
                    \draw[thin] ($(u1) + (\alphaLeaderShiftX,\alphaLeaderShiftY)$) -- ++(\alphaLeaderDx,\alphaLeaderDy) node[below right] {$\frac{4}{3}$};

                    \draw[thin] (betaMax) ++(\betaLeaderShiftX,\betaLeaderShiftY) -- ++(\betaLeaderDx,\betaLeaderDy) node[above right] {$\frac{2}{\sqrt{3}}$};
                    \draw[thin] (betaMax) ++(\betaLeaderShiftX,0) -- ++(-2*\betaLeaderShiftX,0);
                \end{tikzpicture}
                \caption{Maximum achievable $\upalpha\upbeta$-reference with min-max zero-sequence injection}
                \label{fig:zero_injection_three_phase_pwm_alpha_beta_voltage_limit}
            \end{figure}
        \end{column}
    \end{columns}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Proof min-max zero-sequence injection voltage capacity %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Proof min-max zero-sequence injection voltage capacity}
    Using symmetry we will focus on the \hl{first sector} of the hexagon, i.e., $\angle  \bm{s}_{\upalpha\upbeta}\in[\SI{0}{\degree}, \SI{60}{\degree}]$   (cf. \figref{fig:elementary_voltages_alpha_beta}). Any reference voltage in the first sector can be expressed as a linear combination of the two adjacent switching vectors, i.e.,
    \begin{equation}
        \bm{s}_{\upalpha\upbeta} = \frac{\bm{u}_{\upalpha\upbeta}^*}{\nicefrac{u_\mathrm{dc}}{2}} = \tau_1 \bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}1} + \tau_2 \bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}2}, \quad \text{with} \quad \tau_1, \tau_2 \geq 0, \quad \tau_1 + \tau_2 \leq 1.
    \end{equation}
    Here, $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}1}$ and $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}2}$ are the normalized elementary switching vectors of the first sector, i.e.
    \begin{equation}
        \bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}1} = \begin{bmatrix}
            \frac{4}{3} & 0
        \end{bmatrix}^\top, \quad \bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}2} = \begin{bmatrix}
            \frac{2}{3} & \frac{2}{\sqrt{3}}
        \end{bmatrix}^\top.
    \end{equation}
    Hence, the normalized phase voltage references can be found be the inverse Clarke transformation as
    \begin{equation}
        \bm{s}^*_\mathrm{abc} = \begin{bmatrix}
            1                & 0                       \\
            -\nicefrac{1}{2} & \nicefrac{\sqrt{3}}{2}  \\
            -\nicefrac{1}{2} & -\nicefrac{\sqrt{3}}{2}
        \end{bmatrix} \left(\tau_1 \bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}1} + \tau_2 \bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}2}\right) = \begin{bmatrix}
            \nicefrac{4}{3}\tau_1 + \nicefrac{2}{3}\tau_2  \\
            -\nicefrac{2}{3}\tau_1 + \nicefrac{2}{3}\tau_2 \\
            -\nicefrac{2}{3}\tau_1 - \nicefrac{4}{3}\tau_2
        \end{bmatrix}.
        \label{eq:first_sector_hexagon_lin_comb_abc}
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Proof min-max zero-sequence injection voltage capacity (cont.)%%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Proof min-max zero-sequence injection voltage capacity (cont.)}
    With $\tau_1, \tau_2 \geq 0$ it follows directly from \eqref{eq:first_sector_hexagon_lin_comb_abc} that
    \begin{equation}
        s_\mathrm{a}^* \geq s_\mathrm{b}^* \geq s_\mathrm{c}^* \quad \Rightarrow \quad  \max\left\{s_\mathrm{a}^*, s_\mathrm{b}^*, s_\mathrm{c}^*\right\} = s_\mathrm{a}^*, \quad \min\left\{s_\mathrm{a}^*, s_\mathrm{b}^*, s_\mathrm{c}^*\right\} = s_\mathrm{c}^*.
    \end{equation}
    Hence, the zero-sequence injected phase voltage is $s_0 = \nicefrac{1}{2}(s_\mathrm{a}^* + s_\mathrm{c}^*)=\nicefrac{1}{3}(\tau_1 - \tau_2)$ leading to the shifted phase voltage references
    \begin{equation}
        s_\mathrm{a}^{**} = s_\mathrm{a}^* - s_0 = \tau_1 + \tau_2, \quad s_\mathrm{b}^{**} = s_\mathrm{b}^* - s_0 = -\tau_1 + \tau_2, \quad s_\mathrm{c}^{**} = s_\mathrm{c}^* - s_0 = -\tau_1 -\tau_2.
        \label{eq:shifted_three_phase_PWM_modulation_indices_min_max}
    \end{equation}
    Because of $\tau_1 + \tau_2 \leq 1$ we have
    \begin{equation}
        |s_\mathrm{a}^{**}| \leq 1, \quad |s_\mathrm{b}^{**}| \leq 1, \quad |s_\mathrm{c}^{**}| \leq 1,
    \end{equation}
    i.e., \hl{each phase voltage reference stays within the linear modulation range and is realizable}. The transfer to other sectors of the hexagon is straightforward by symmetry.
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Three-phase PWM with zero-sequence injection %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Three-phase PWM with zero-sequence injection}
    \begin{figure}
        \begin{circuitikz}[x=1cm,y=1cm]
            \def\cwidth{1.15}
            \def\cheight{0.9}
            \def\rowsep{1.75}

            \node[adder] (shift1) at (3.05,0) {};
            \node[adder] (shift2) at (4.05,-\rowsep) {};
            \node[adder] (shift3) at (5.05,-2*\rowsep) {};

            \node[adder] (add1) at (6.05,0) {};
            \node[adder] (add2) at (7.05,-\rowsep) {};
            \node[adder] (add3) at (8.05,-2*\rowsep) {};

            \node[ctrlblock, minimum width = \cwidth cm, minimum height = \cheight cm] (comp1) at (9.55,0) {};
            \node[ctrlblock, minimum width = \cwidth cm, minimum height = \cheight cm] (comp2) at (9.55,-\rowsep) {};
            \node[ctrlblock, minimum width = \cwidth cm, minimum height = \cheight cm] (comp3) at (9.55,-2*\rowsep) {};

            \coordinate (zeroCenter) at ($(shift2) + (0,-3.2)$);
            \coordinate (carrierCenter) at ($(add2) + (0,-3.2)$);
            \node[ctrlblock, minimum width = 1.35 cm, minimum height = \cheight cm] (zero) at (zeroCenter) {$s_0(t)$};
            \node[ctrlblock, minimum width = \cwidth cm, minimum height = \cheight cm] (carrier) at (carrierCenter) {};

            \coordinate (zeroInB) at ($(zero.north west)!0.50!(zero.south west)$);
            \coordinate (zeroInC) at ($(zero.north west)!0.78!(zero.south west)$);
            \path (carrier.south west) coordinate (blockBottomLeft);

            \draw[->] (0,0) -- coordinate[pos=0.42] (tap1) node[above]{$s_\mathrm{a}^*(t)$} (shift1.west);
            \draw[->] (0,-\rowsep) -- coordinate[pos=0.42] (tap2) node[above]{$s_\mathrm{b}^*(t)$} (shift2.west);
            \draw[->] (0,-2*\rowsep) -- coordinate[pos=0.42] (tap3) node[above]{$s_\mathrm{c}^*(t)$} (shift3.west);
            \node[crossingshape, name=jumpAB, rotate=-90] at (tap1 |- shift2.west) {};
            \node[crossingshape, name=jumpAC, rotate=-90] at (tap1 |- shift3.west) {};
            \node[crossingshape, name=jumpBC, rotate=-90] at (tap2 |- shift3.west) {};

            \fill (tap1) circle (1.1pt);
            \fill (tap2) circle (1.1pt);
            \fill (tap3) circle (1.1pt);

            \draw (tap1) -- (jumpAB.west);
            \draw (jumpAB.east) -- (jumpAC.west);
            \draw (jumpAC.east) |- (zeroInA);
            \draw (tap2) -- (jumpBC.west);
            \draw (jumpBC.east) |- (zeroInB);
            \draw (tap3) |- (zeroInC);

            \node[crossingshape, name=jumpZab, rotate=-90] at (shift1.south |- shift2.west) {};
            \node[crossingshape, name=jumpZac, rotate=-90] at (shift1.south |- shift3.west) {};
            \node[crossingshape, name=jumpZbc, rotate=-90] at (shift2.south |- shift3.west) {};

            \coordinate (zeroOut) at ($(zero.north) + (0,0.25)$);
            \coordinate (zeroStemA) at (shift1.south |- zeroOut);
            \draw (zero.north) -- (zeroOut);
            \fill (zeroOut) circle (1.1pt);
            \draw (zeroOut) -- (zeroStemA);
            \draw (zeroStemA) -- (jumpZac.east);
            \draw (jumpZac.west) -- (jumpZab.east);
            \draw[->] (jumpZab.west) -- (shift1.south);
            \draw (zeroOut) -- (jumpZbc.east);
            \draw[->] (jumpZbc.west) -- (shift2.south);
            \draw[->] (zeroOut) -| (shift3.south);
            \node[anchor = north west] at (shift1.south) {$-$};
            \node[anchor = north west] at (shift2.south) {$-$};
            \node[anchor = north west] at (shift3.south) {$-$};

            \draw[->] (shift1.east) -- node[above, fill=white, inner sep=1pt, yshift=1mm]{$s_\mathrm{a}^{**}(t)$} (add1.west);
            \draw[->] (shift2.east) -- node[above, fill=white, inner sep=1pt, yshift=1mm]{$s_\mathrm{b}^{**}(t)$} (add2.west);
            \draw[->] (shift3.east) -- node[above, fill=white, inner sep=1pt, yshift=1mm]{$s_\mathrm{c}^{**}(t)$} (add3.west);

            \node[crossingshape, name=jumpBab, rotate=-90] at (add1.south |- shift2.east) {};
            \node[crossingshape, name=jumpCab, rotate=-90] at (add1.south |- shift3.east) {};
            \node[crossingshape, name=jumpCbc, rotate=-90] at (add2.south |- shift3.east) {};

            \coordinate (carrierOut) at ($(carrier.north) + (0,0.25)$);
            \draw (carrier.north) -- (carrierOut);
            \fill (carrierOut) circle (1.1pt);
            \coordinate (carrierStemA) at (add1.south |- carrierOut);
            \draw (carrierOut) -- (carrierStemA);
            \draw (carrierStemA) -- (jumpCab.east);
            \draw (jumpCab.west) -- (jumpBab.east);
            \draw[->] (jumpBab.west) -- (add1.south);
            \draw (carrierOut) -- (jumpCbc.east);
            \draw[->] (jumpCbc.west) -- node[pos=0.50, right] {$c(t)$} (add2.south);
            \draw[->] (carrierOut) -| (add3.south);
            \node[anchor = north west] at (add1.south) {$-$};
            \node[anchor = north west] at (add2.south) {$-$};
            \node[anchor = north west] at (add3.south) {$-$};

            \draw[->] (add1.east) -- (comp1.west);
            \draw[->] (add2.east) -- (comp2.west);
            \draw[->] (add3.east) -- (comp3.west);

            % Triangular signal pattern within carrier block
            \begin{scope}
                \def\signalsteps{6}
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\stepwidth}{\cwidth/\signalsteps}
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\signalheight}{\cheight/1.3}

                \draw[black, thick]
                ($(blockBottomLeft) + (0.025, 0.1*\cheight)$)
                \foreach \x in {1,...,\signalsteps} {
                        -- ($
                            (blockBottomLeft) +
                            (\x*\stepwidth, {0.1*\cheight + mod(\x, 2)*\signalheight})
                        $)
                    };
            \end{scope}

            % Comparator block #1
            \begin{axis}[at={(comp1)}, scale only axis, width = 0.8*\cwidth cm, height = 0.8*\cheight cm, anchor = center, xtick=\empty, ytick={0,1}, axis lines=middle, ymax=1.25, ymin = -1.25, font = \footnotesize, extra y ticks={-1}, extra y tick style = {yticklabel shift = -0.75cm}]
                \addplot[thick, signalalpha] coordinates {(-1,-1) (0,-1) (0,1) (1,1)};
            \end{axis}
            % Comparator block #2

                \addplot[thick, signalalpha] coordinates {(-1,-1) (0,-1) (0,1) (1,1)};
            \end{axis}
            % Comparator block #3
            \begin{axis}[at={(comp3)}, scale only axis, width = 0.8*\cwidth cm, height = 0.8*\cheight cm, anchor = center, xtick=\empty, ytick={0,1}, axis lines=middle, ymax=1.25, ymin = -1.25, font = \footnotesize, extra y ticks={-1}, extra y tick style = {yticklabel shift = -0.75cm}]
                \addplot[thick, signalalpha] coordinates {(-1,-1) (0,-1) (0,1) (1,1)};
            \end{axis}

            \draw[->] (comp1.east) -- ++(0.95,0) node[anchor = west]{$s_\mathrm{a}(t)$};
            \draw[->] (comp2.east) -- ++(0.95,0) node[anchor = west]{$s_\mathrm{b}(t)$};
            \draw[->] (comp3.east) -- ++(0.95,0) node[anchor = west]{$s_\mathrm{c}(t)$};
        \end{circuitikz}
        \caption{Three-phase PWM with zero-sequence injection}
        \label{fig:three-phase_pwm_with_zero_sequence_injection}
    \end{figure}

    \begin{figure}

            \pgfplotsset{table/search path={fig/lec02}}

                % Top plot: original normalized voltage references

                \addplot[signalalpha, thick] table[x=wt, y=d_a, col sep=comma] {PWM_three-phase_zero_injection_mod115_example.csv};
                \addplot[signalbeta, thick] table[x=wt, y=d_b, col sep=comma] {PWM_three-phase_zero_injection_mod115_example.csv};
                \addplot[signalgamma, thick] table[x=wt, y=d_c, col sep=comma] {PWM_three-phase_zero_injection_mod115_example.csv};
                \node[signalalpha, anchor=north, fill = white, inner sep = 1pt] at (axis cs: pi/2, 0.95) {\small $s_\mathrm{a}^*$};
                \node[signalbeta, anchor=north, fill = white, inner sep = 1pt] at (axis cs: 7*pi/6, 0.95) {\small $s_\mathrm{b}^*$};
                \node[signalgamma, anchor=north, fill = white, inner sep = 1pt] at (axis cs: 11*pi/6, 0.95) {\small $s_\mathrm{c}^*$};

                % middle plot: injected duty cycles and carrier
                \nextgroupplot[ylabel = {$s_i^{**}(t), c(t)$}]
                \addplot[signalalpha, thick] table[x=wt, y=d_a_mod, col sep=comma] {PWM_three-phase_zero_injection_mod115_example.csv};
                \addplot[signalbeta, thick] table[x=wt, y=d_b_mod, col sep=comma] {PWM_three-phase_zero_injection_mod115_example.csv};
                \addplot[signalgamma, thick] table[x=wt, y=d_c_mod, col sep=comma] {PWM_three-phase_zero_injection_mod115_example.csv};
                \addplot[black, thick] table[x=wt, y=c, col sep=comma] {PWM_three-phase_zero_injection_mod115_example.csv};
                \node[signalalpha, anchor=north, fill = white, inner sep = 0.1pt] at (axis cs: pi/2, 0.70) {\small $s_\mathrm{a}^{**}$};
                \node[signalbeta, anchor=north, fill = white, inner sep = 0.1pt] at (axis cs: 6.6*pi/6, 0.7) {\small $s_\mathrm{b}^{**}$};
                \node[signalgamma, anchor=north, fill = white, inner sep = 0.1pt] at (axis cs: 11.4*pi/6, 0.7) {\small $s_\mathrm{c}^{**}$};
                \node[black, anchor=center] at (axis cs: 0.3, -0.4) {\small $c$};

                % switching sequence phase a
                \nextgroupplot[ylabel = {$s_\mathrm{a}(t)$}, height=0.26\textheight, ytick={-1,1}, yticklabels={$-1$,$+1$}, ymin = -1.25, ymax =1.25]
                \addplot[signalalpha, thick] table[x=wt, y=sa, col sep=comma] {PWM_three-phase_zero_injection_mod115_example.csv};

                % switching sequence phase b
                \nextgroupplot[ylabel = {$s_\mathrm{b}(t)$}, height=0.26\textheight, ytick={-1,1}, yticklabels={$-1$,$+1$}, ymin = -1.25, ymax =1.25]
                \addplot[signalbeta, thick] table[x=wt, y=sb, col sep=comma] {PWM_three-phase_zero_injection_mod115_example.csv};

                % switching sequence phase c
                \nextgroupplot[ylabel = {$s_\mathrm{c}(t)$}, xlabel={$\omega t$}, xlabel style={yshift=1ex}, height=0.26\textheight, ytick={-1,1}, yticklabels={$-1$,$+1$}, ymin = -1.25, ymax =1.25]
                \addplot[signalgamma, thick] table[x=wt, y=sc, col sep=comma] {PWM_three-phase_zero_injection_mod115_example.csv};
            \end{groupplot}
        \end{tikzpicture}
    \end{figure}
\end{frame}


%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\subsection{Three-phase overmodulation}
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Overmodulation for three-phase PWM with min-max injection %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Overmodulation for three-phase PWM with min-max injection}
    \begin{columns}[onlytextwidth]
        \begin{column}{0.53\textwidth}
            Beyond $m^* > \nicefrac{2}{\sqrt{3}}$ the phase voltage references leave the linear modulation range and are no longer realizable. The resulting overmodulation strategy is a simple \hl{clipping}, i.e.,
            \begin{equation}
                \begin{split}
                    s_{i}^{**}(t)          & = \operatorname{clip}\!\left(s_{i}^{*}(t)-s_0(t)\right), \\
                    \operatorname{clip}(x) & = \min\!\left\{1,\max\!\left\{-1,x\right\}\right\}.
                \end{split}
            \end{equation}
            \begin{varblock}{Control disturbance}
                The clipping renders itself a control disturbance and reduces the degrees of freedom: in the linear range, amplitude and phase of the voltage reference can be controlled independently, while in the overmodulation range those two are coupled.
            \end{varblock}
        \end{column}
        \begin{column}{0.45\textwidth}
            \vspace{-0.2cm}
            \begin{figure}
                \begin{tikzpicture}[x=1.2cm,y=1.2cm,>=Latex]
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\outerRadius}{2}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\mStar}{1.24}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\commandedRadius}{1.5*\mStar}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\clipGamma}{acos(2/(sqrt(3)*\mStar))}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\innerRadius}{sqrt(3)}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\tickHalf}{0.08}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\alphaLeaderShiftX}{0.03}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\alphaLeaderShiftY}{-0.15}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\alphaLeaderDx}{0.10}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\alphaLeaderDy}{-0.28}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\betaLeaderShiftX}{0.08}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\betaLeaderShiftY}{0.08}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\betaLeaderDx}{0.35}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\betaLeaderDy}{0.20}
                    \coordinate (O) at (0,0);
                    \foreach \name/\angle in {u1/0,u2/60,u3/120,u4/180,u5/240,u6/300} {
                            \coordinate (\name) at (\angle:\outerRadius);
                        }
                    \coordinate (betaMax) at (90:\innerRadius);
                    \draw[gray!70,thick] (u1)--(u2)--(u3)--(u4)--(u5)--(u6)--cycle;
                    \draw[signalalpha,dotted,thick] (O) circle [radius=\commandedRadius];
                    \draw[->,thin] (-2.25,0) -- (2.25,0) node[right] {$s_\upalpha^*$};
                    \draw[->,thin] (0,-2.15) -- (0,2.15) node[above] {$s_\upbeta^*$};

                    \draw[thin] (u1) ++(0,\tickHalf) -- ++(0,-2*\tickHalf);
                    \draw[thin] ($(u1) + (\alphaLeaderShiftX,\alphaLeaderShiftY)$) -- ++(\alphaLeaderDx,\alphaLeaderDy) node[below right] {$\frac{4}{3}$};

                    \draw[thin] (betaMax) ++(\betaLeaderShiftX,\betaLeaderShiftY) -- ++(\betaLeaderDx,\betaLeaderDy) node[above right] {$\frac{2}{\sqrt{3}}$};
                    \draw[thin] (betaMax) ++(\betaLeaderShiftX,0) -- ++(-2*\betaLeaderShiftX,0);

                    \foreach \sector in {0,...,5} {
                            \pgfmathsetmacro{\sectorCenter}{30 + 60*\sector}
                            \pgfmathsetmacro{\clipStart}{\sectorCenter - \clipGamma}
                            \pgfmathsetmacro{\clipEnd}{\sectorCenter + \clipGamma}
                            \pgfmathsetmacro{\nextArcEnd}{\sectorCenter + 60 - \clipGamma}

                            \draw[signalbeta,dashed,thick] (\clipStart:\commandedRadius) -- (\clipEnd:\commandedRadius);
                            \draw[signalbeta,dashed,thick] (\clipEnd:\commandedRadius) arc[start angle=\clipEnd,end angle=\nextArcEnd,radius=\commandedRadius];
                        }

                    \node[signalalpha, fill=white, inner sep=1pt, right, align=left] at (1.86,1.22) {\scriptsize reference\\[-2pt]\scriptsize $m^*=1.24$};
                    \node[signalbeta, fill=white, inner sep=1pt, left] at (1.54,0.64) {\scriptsize clipping};
                \end{tikzpicture}
                \caption{Beyond $m^*=\nicefrac{2}{\sqrt{3}}$, the desired sinusoidal trajectory leaves the linear range and is clipped at the inverter hexagon.}
                \label{fig:min_max_injection_overmodulation_hexagon_clipping}
            \end{figure}
        \end{column}
    \end{columns}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Min-max injection clipping law %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Min-max injection clipping law in the first hexagon sector}
    Assume the balanced sinusoidal reference vector
    \begin{equation}
        s_\mathrm{a}^*(\theta)=m^*\cos\theta, \qquad
        s_\mathrm{b}^*(\theta)=m^*\cos\!\left(\theta-\frac{2\pi}{3}\right), \qquad
        s_\mathrm{c}^*(\theta)=m^*\cos\!\left(\theta+\frac{2\pi}{3}\right).
        \label{eq:balanced_sinusoidal_reference_PWM}
    \end{equation}
    In the first sector ($0 \le \theta \le \nicefrac{\pi}{3}$), the min-max injected zero-sequence is
    \begin{equation}
        \begin{split}
            s_0(\theta) & = \frac{1}{2}\left(\max\{s_\mathrm{a}^*(\theta), s_\mathrm{b}^*(\theta), s_\mathrm{c}^*(\theta)\} + \min\{s_\mathrm{a}^*(\theta), s_\mathrm{b}^*(\theta), s_\mathrm{c}^*(\theta)\}\right) \\
                        & = \frac{1}{2}\left(s_\mathrm{a}^*(\theta) + s_\mathrm{c}^*(\theta)\right)= \frac{m^*}{2}\cos\!\left(\theta+\frac{\pi}{3}\right), \quad \text{for} \quad 0 \le \theta \le \frac{\pi}{3}.
        \end{split}
    \end{equation}
    Hence, the unclipped injected voltage references for the first sector are
    \begin{equation}
        \begin{split}
            s_\mathrm{a}^*(\theta) - s_0(\theta) & = m^*\cos\theta - \frac{m^*}{2}\cos\!\left(\theta+\frac{\pi}{3}\right) = \frac{\sqrt{3}m^*}{2}\cos\!\left(\theta-\frac{\pi}{6}\right),                                \\
            s_\mathrm{b}^*(\theta) - s_0(\theta) & = m^*\cos\!\left(\theta-\frac{2\pi}{3}\right) - \frac{m^*}{2}\cos\!\left(\theta+\frac{\pi}{3}\right) = \frac{3m^*}{2}\cos\!\left(\theta-\frac{2\pi}{3}\right),        \\
            s_\mathrm{c}^*(\theta) - s_0(\theta) & = m^*\cos\!\left(\theta+\frac{2\pi}{3}\right) - \frac{m^*}{2}\cos\!\left(\theta+\frac{\pi}{3}\right) = \frac{\sqrt{3}m^*}{2}\cos\!\left(\theta+\frac{5\pi}{6}\right).
        \end{split}
        \label{eq:unclipped_ref_overmod_min_max}
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Min-max injection clipping law %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Min-max injection clipping law in the first hexagon sector (cont.)}
    The cosine terms in \eqref{eq:unclipped_ref_overmod_min_max} have the following maximum absolute values in the first sector:
    \begin{equation}
        \left|\cos\left(\theta - \frac{\pi}{6}\right)\right|  \leq 1,                                                                                     \quad
        \left|\cos\left(\theta - \frac{2\pi}{3}\right)\right|  \leq \frac{1}{2},       \quad
        \left|\cos\left(\theta + \frac{5\pi}{6}\right)\right|  \leq 1, \quad \text{for} \quad 0 \le \theta \le \frac{\pi}{3}.
    \end{equation}
    Since phases $\mathrm{a}$ and $\mathrm{c}$ are symmetric, we can distinguish two cases:
    \begin{equation}
        \max_\theta \left\{|s_\mathrm{a}^*- s_0|, |s_\mathrm{c}^*- s_0|\right\} = \frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}m^* \quad \text{and} \quad \max_\theta |s_\mathrm{b}^*- s_0| = \frac{3}{2}\cdot\frac{1}{2}m^* = \frac{3}{4}m^*.
    \end{equation}
    Hence, in terms of overmodulation clipping we have two regions:
    \begin{itemize}
        \item \textbf{Region I: \(\nicefrac{2}{\sqrt{3}} < m^* \le \nicefrac{4}{3}\)}\\
              Only phases $\mathrm{a}$ and $\mathrm{c}$ are clipped, while phase $\mathrm{b}$ is still realizable without clipping.
        \item \textbf{Region II: \(m^* \ge \nicefrac{4}{3}\)}\\
              All three phases are clipped.
    \end{itemize}
    In order to derive the fundamental voltage amplitude, we need to determine the clipping intervals for those two regions.
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Min-max injection clipping law %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Min-max injection clipping law in the first hexagon sector (region I)}
    In region I, clipping starts and ends at the two first-sector roots of
    \begin{equation}
        \cos\left(\theta - \frac{\pi}{6}\right) = \frac{2}{\sqrt{3}m^*}, \qquad \text{for} \qquad \frac{2}{\sqrt{3}} < m^* \le \frac{4}{3}, \quad 0 \le \theta \le \frac{\pi}{3}.
    \end{equation}
    Since the cosine is symmetric around $\theta = \nicefrac{\pi}{6}$, the clipping interval boundaries are
    \begin{equation}
        \gamma_1 = \frac{\pi}{6} - \arccos\!\left(\frac{2}{\sqrt{3}m^*}\right),
        \qquad
        \gamma_2 = \frac{\pi}{6} + \arccos\!\left(\frac{2}{\sqrt{3}m^*}\right).
    \end{equation}
    Hence, phases $\mathrm{a}$ and $\mathrm{c}$ are clipped for $\theta \in [\gamma_1,\gamma_2]$ with clipping width
    \begin{equation}
        \Delta\gamma = \gamma_2 - \gamma_1 = 2\arccos\!\left(\frac{2}{\sqrt{3}m^*}\right).
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Min-max injection clipping law %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Min-max injection clipping law in the first hexagon sector (region I, cont.)}
    \begin{figure}
        \centering
        \begin{tikzpicture}[x=1.75cm,y=1.75cm,>=Latex]
            \pgfmathsetmacro{\outerRadius}{2}
            \pgfmathsetmacro{\mStar}{1.22}
            \pgfmathsetmacro{\referenceStartAngle}{-20}
            \pgfmathsetmacro{\referenceEndAngle}{95}
            \pgfmathsetmacro{\gammaDelta}{acos(2/(sqrt(3)*\mStar))}
            \pgfmathsetmacro{\gammaOneAngle}{30 - \gammaDelta}
            \pgfmathsetmacro{\gammaTwoAngle}{30 + \gammaDelta}
            \pgfmathsetmacro{\lowerAdjReleaseAngle}{-30 + \gammaDelta}
            \pgfmathsetmacro{\upperAdjEngageAngle}{90 - \gammaDelta}
            \pgfmathsetmacro{\commandedRadius}{2/(cos(\gammaTwoAngle) + sin(\gammaTwoAngle)/sqrt(3))}
            \pgfmathsetmacro{\deltaGammaArcRadius}{0.70}
            \pgfmathsetmacro{\referenceLabelRadiusFactor}{0.98}
            \pgfmathsetmacro{\referenceLabelOffset}{0.22}
            \pgfmathsetmacro{\clippedLabelOffset}{0.28}

            \coordinate (O) at (0,0);
            \coordinate (u1) at (0:\outerRadius);
            \coordinate (u2) at (60:\outerRadius);
            \coordinate (u2prev) at ($(u2)+(-1.35,0)$);
            \coordinate (u1next) at ($(u1)+(240:0.78)$);
            \coordinate (refStart) at (\referenceStartAngle:\commandedRadius);
            \coordinate (refEnd) at (\referenceEndAngle:\commandedRadius);
            \coordinate (clipStart) at (\gammaOneAngle:\commandedRadius);
            \coordinate (clipEnd) at (\gammaTwoAngle:\commandedRadius);
            \coordinate (referenceLabelBase) at (30:{\referenceLabelRadiusFactor*\commandedRadius});
            \coordinate (referenceLabelPos) at ($(referenceLabelBase)+(-60:\referenceLabelOffset)$);
            \coordinate (clipLabelBase) at ($(clipStart)!0.5!(clipEnd)$);
            \coordinate (clipLabelPos) at ($(clipLabelBase)+(210:\clippedLabelOffset)$);
            \coordinate (lowerAdjClipStart) at ({2*sqrt(3)*cos(\referenceStartAngle)/(sqrt(3)*cos(\referenceStartAngle)-sin(\referenceStartAngle))},{2*sqrt(3)*sin(\referenceStartAngle)/(sqrt(3)*cos(\referenceStartAngle)-sin(\referenceStartAngle))});
            \coordinate (lowerAdjClipEnd) at ({2*sqrt(3)*cos(\lowerAdjReleaseAngle)/(sqrt(3)*cos(\lowerAdjReleaseAngle)-sin(\lowerAdjReleaseAngle))},{2*sqrt(3)*sin(\lowerAdjReleaseAngle)/(sqrt(3)*cos(\lowerAdjReleaseAngle)-sin(\lowerAdjReleaseAngle))});
            \coordinate (upperAdjClipStart) at ({sqrt(3)*cos(\upperAdjEngageAngle)/sin(\upperAdjEngageAngle)},{sqrt(3)});
            \coordinate (upperAdjClipEnd) at ({sqrt(3)*cos(\referenceEndAngle)/sin(\referenceEndAngle)},{sqrt(3)});

            \draw[->,thin] (O) -- (2.35,0) node[right] {$s_\upalpha^*$};
            \draw[->,thin] (O) -- (0,2.3) node[above] {$s_\upbeta^*$};
            \draw[gray!60,->,thin] (O) -- (u1) node[below right, gray!60, fill=white, inner sep=0.1pt, yshift=-3pt] {\scriptsize $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}1}$};
            \draw[gray!60,->,thin] (O) -- (u2) node[above right, gray!60, fill=white, inner sep=0.1pt] {\scriptsize $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}2}$};
            \draw[gray!70,thick] (u1) -- (u2);
            \draw[gray!70,dashed,thick] (u2prev) -- (u2);
            \draw[gray!70,dashed,thick] (u1) -- (u1next);

            \draw[signalalpha,dotted,thick] (refStart) arc[start angle=\referenceStartAngle,end angle=\referenceEndAngle,radius=\commandedRadius];
            \draw[signalbeta,dashed,very thick] (lowerAdjClipStart) -- (lowerAdjClipEnd);
            \draw[signalbeta,dashed,very thick] (lowerAdjClipEnd) arc[start angle=\lowerAdjReleaseAngle,end angle=\gammaOneAngle,radius=\commandedRadius];
            \draw[signalbeta,dashed,very thick] (clipStart) -- (clipEnd);
            \draw[signalbeta,dashed,very thick] (clipEnd) arc[start angle=\gammaTwoAngle,end angle=\upperAdjEngageAngle,radius=\commandedRadius];
            \draw[signalbeta,dashed,very thick] (upperAdjClipStart) -- (upperAdjClipEnd);

            \draw[thin,dashed] (O) -- (clipStart);
            \draw[thin,dashed] (O) -- (clipEnd);
            \draw[thin] (\gammaOneAngle:\deltaGammaArcRadius) arc[start angle=\gammaOneAngle,end angle=\gammaTwoAngle,radius=\deltaGammaArcRadius];

            \fill[signalbeta] (clipStart) circle (1.4pt);
            \fill[signalbeta] (clipEnd) circle (1.4pt);

            \node[fill=white, inner sep=0.1pt, yshift=3pt, xshift=3pt] at (0.76,0.38) {\scriptsize $\Delta\gamma$};
            \node[signalalpha, fill=white, inner sep=0.1pt, align=left, above right, xshift=2pt, yshift=1pt] at (referenceLabelPos) {\scriptsize reference\\[-2pt]\scriptsize $m^*=1.22$};
            \node[signalbeta, fill=white, inner sep=0.1pt, xshift=-2pt, yshift=-1pt] at (clipLabelPos) {\scriptsize clipping};
        \end{tikzpicture}
        \caption{Zoom into the upper-right quadrant of the $\upalpha\upbeta$ plane visualizing the clipping interval -- calculations for the other sectors are symmetric and can be obtained by appropriate angle shifts.}
        \label{fig:min_max_injection_region1_gamma_definition}
    \end{figure}
\end{frame}


%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Min-max injection clipping law in the first hexagon sector (region I, cont.) %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Min-max injection clipping law in the first hexagon sector (region I, cont.)}
    Let
    \begin{equation}
        \underline{s}^{**}(\theta) = s_{\upalpha}^{**}(\theta) + \mathrm{j}s_{\upbeta}^{**}(\theta)
    \end{equation}
    denote the clipped realized normalized voltage vector. Then the positive-sequence fundamental amplitude follows from the first Fourier coefficient as
    \begin{equation}
        m^{(1)} = \left|\frac{1}{2\pi}\int_{0}^{2\pi} \underline{s}^{**}(\theta)e^{-\mathrm{j}\theta}\,\mathrm{d}\theta\right|.
    \end{equation}
    With six-sector symmetry, it is sufficient to integrate over sector 1 only:
    \begin{equation}
        m^{(1)} = \frac{3}{\pi}\int_{0}^{\pi/3} \Re\!\left\{\underline{s}^{**}(\theta)e^{-\mathrm{j}\theta}\right\}\,\mathrm{d}\theta.
    \end{equation}
    Here, $\Re\{\cdot\}$ denotes the real part. In region I, sector 1 splits into $[0,\gamma_1] \cup [\gamma_1,\gamma_2] \cup [\gamma_2,\pi/3]$.
    On the two outer intervals, the realizable vector equals the commanded one,
    \begin{equation}
        \underline{s}^{**}(\theta) = m^*e^{\mathrm{j}\theta}
        \quad \Rightarrow \quad
        \Re\!\left\{\underline{s}^{**}(\theta)e^{-\mathrm{j}\theta}\right\} = m^*.
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Min-max injection clipping law in the first hexagon sector (region I, cont.) %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Min-max injection clipping law in the first hexagon sector (region I, cont.)}
    Hence, only the clipped interval contributes a nontrivial correction:
    \begin{equation}
        m^{(1)} = \frac{3}{\pi}\left[m^*\left(\frac{\pi}{3}-\Delta\gamma\right) + \int_{\gamma_1}^{\gamma_2} \Re\!\left\{\underline{s}^{**}(\theta)e^{-\mathrm{j}\theta}\right\}\,\mathrm{d}\theta\right].
    \end{equation}
    On the clipped interval we have $s_\mathrm{a}^{**}=1$, $s_\mathrm{c}^{**}=-1$, and with $\psi=\theta-\nicefrac{\pi}{6}$,
    \begin{equation}
        s_\mathrm{b}^{**} = \frac{3m^*}{2}\sin\psi.
    \end{equation}
    Applying the Clarke transformation yields
    \begin{equation}
        s_{\upalpha}^{**}(\theta) = 1 - \frac{m^*}{2}\sin\psi,
        \qquad
        s_{\upbeta}^{**}(\theta) = \frac{1}{\sqrt{3}} + \frac{\sqrt{3}m^*}{2}\sin\psi.
    \end{equation}
    Therefore,
    \begin{equation}
        \Re\!\left\{\underline{s}^{**}(\theta)e^{-\mathrm{j}\theta}\right\}
        = s_{\upalpha}^{**}(\theta)\cos\theta + s_{\upbeta}^{**}(\theta)\sin\theta
        = \frac{2}{\sqrt{3}}\cos\psi + m^*\sin^2\psi.
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Min-max injection clipping law in the first hexagon sector (region I, cont.) %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Min-max injection clipping law in the first hexagon sector (region I, cont.)}
    Since the clipping interval is symmetric around $\nicefrac{\pi}{6}$ and has width $\Delta\gamma = \gamma_2-\gamma_1$, the shifted variable satisfies $\psi \in [-\nicefrac{\Delta\gamma}{2},\nicefrac{\Delta\gamma}{2}]$, giving
    \begin{equation}
        m^{(1)} = \frac{3}{\pi}\left[m^*\left(\frac{\pi}{3}-\Delta\gamma\right) + \int_{-\nicefrac{\Delta\gamma}{2}}^{\nicefrac{\Delta\gamma}{2}}\left(\frac{2}{\sqrt{3}}\cos\psi + m^*\sin^2\psi\right)\mathrm{d}\psi\right].
    \end{equation}
    After integration, this becomes
    \begin{equation}
        \begin{split}
            m^{(1)} & = \frac{3}{\pi}\left[m^*\frac{\pi}{3} - \frac{m^*}{2}\Delta\gamma - \frac{m^*}{2}\sin\!\left(\Delta\gamma\right) + \frac{4}{\sqrt{3}}\sin\!\left(\frac{\Delta\gamma}{2}\right)\right] \\
                    & = m^* - \frac{3m^*}{2\pi}\Delta\gamma - \frac{3m^*}{2\pi}\sin\!\left(\Delta\gamma\right) + \frac{4\sqrt{3}}{\pi}\sin\!\left(\frac{\Delta\gamma}{2}\right).
        \end{split}
    \end{equation}
    With $\Delta\gamma = 2\arccos\!\left(\frac{2}{\sqrt{3}m^*}\right)$, we receive the final expression for the fundamental modulation amplitude in region I:
    \begin{equation}
        m^{(1)} = m^* - \frac{3m^*}{\pi}\arccos\!\left(\frac{2}{\sqrt{3}m^*}\right) + \frac{2\sqrt{3}}{\pi}\sqrt{1-\frac{4}{3(m^*)^2}}, \quad \text{for} \quad \frac{2}{\sqrt{3}} < m^* \le \frac{4}{3}.
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Min-max injection clipping law in the first hexagon sector (region II) %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Min-max injection clipping law in the first hexagon sector (region II)}
    In region II, i.e. for $m^* \geq \nicefrac{4}{3}$, phases $\mathrm{a}$ and $\mathrm{c}$ are clipped over the entire first sector.
    Phase $\mathrm{b}$ is unclipped only between the two roots of
    \begin{equation}
        \left|\frac{3m^*}{2}\sin\!\left(\theta-\frac{\pi}{6}\right)\right| = 1,
        \qquad 0 \leq \theta \leq \frac{\pi}{3}.
    \end{equation}
    By symmetry around $\nicefrac{\pi}{6}$, the interval boundaries are
    \begin{equation}
        \delta_1 = \frac{\pi}{6} - \arcsin\!\left(\frac{2}{3m^*}\right),
        \qquad
        \delta_2 = \frac{\pi}{6} + \arcsin\!\left(\frac{2}{3m^*}\right),
    \end{equation}
    with unclipped width
    \begin{equation}
        \Delta\delta = \delta_2 - \delta_1 = 2\arcsin\!\left(\frac{2}{3m^*}\right).
    \end{equation}
    Hence, $s_\mathrm{b}^{**}=-1$ on $[0,\delta_1]$, $s_\mathrm{b}^{**}=+1$ on $[\delta_2,\nicefrac{\pi}{3}]$, and only on $[\delta_1,\delta_2]$ phase $\mathrm{b}$ remains unclipped.
\end{frame}


%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Min-max injection clipping law in the first hexagon sector (region II, cont.) %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Min-max injection clipping law in the first hexagon sector (region II, cont.)}
    Therefore, the realized space vector is piecewise given by
    \begin{equation}
        \underline{s}^{**}(\theta) =
        \begin{cases}
            \nicefrac{4}{3},                                                & 0 \leq \theta \leq \delta_1,                 \\
            s_{\upalpha}^{**}(\theta) + \mathrm{j}s_{\upbeta}^{**}(\theta), & \delta_1 \leq \theta \leq \delta_2,          \\
            \nicefrac{2}{3} + \mathrm{j}\nicefrac{2}{\sqrt{3}},             & \delta_2 \leq \theta \leq \nicefrac{\pi}{3},
        \end{cases}
    \end{equation}
    where on the middle interval the same edge relation as in region I applies:
    \begin{equation}
        \Re\!\left\{\underline{s}^{**}(\theta)e^{-\mathrm{j}\theta}\right\}
        = \frac{2}{\sqrt{3}}\cos\psi + m^*\sin^2\psi,
        \qquad \psi = \theta - \frac{\pi}{6}.
    \end{equation}
    Hence,
    \begin{equation}
        \begin{split}
            m^{(1)} = \frac{3}{\pi}\Bigg[ & \int_{0}^{\delta_1} \frac{4}{3}\cos\theta\,\mathrm{d}\theta
            + \int_{-\nicefrac{\Delta\delta}{2}}^{\nicefrac{\Delta\delta}{2}}\left(\frac{2}{\sqrt{3}}\cos\psi + m^*\sin^2\psi\right)\mathrm{d}\psi                        \\
                                          & + \int_{\delta_2}^{\nicefrac{\pi}{3}}\left(\frac{2}{3}\cos\theta + \frac{2}{\sqrt{3}}\sin\theta\right)\mathrm{d}\theta\Bigg].
        \end{split}
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Min-max injection clipping law in the first hexagon sector (region II, cont.) %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Min-max injection clipping law in the first hexagon sector (region II, cont.)}
    Evaluating the integrals and using $\delta_1 = \nicefrac{\pi}{6} - \nicefrac{\Delta\delta}{2}$ gives
    \begin{equation}
        m^{(1)} = \frac{3}{\pi}\left[\frac{4}{3}\cos\!\left(\frac{\Delta\delta}{2}\right) + \frac{m^*}{2}\Delta\delta - \frac{m^*}{2}\sin\!\left(\Delta\delta\right)\right].
    \end{equation}
    Hence, the achievable fundamental modulation amplitude in region II is
    \begin{equation}
        m^{(1)} = \frac{4}{\pi}\cos\!\left(\frac{\Delta\delta}{2}\right) + \frac{3m^*}{2\pi}\Delta\delta - \frac{3m^*}{2\pi}\sin\!\left(\Delta\delta\right).
    \end{equation}
    With $\Delta\delta = 2\arcsin\!\left(\frac{2}{3m^*}\right)$, this becomes
    \begin{equation}
        m^{(1)} = \frac{3m^*}{\pi}\arcsin\!\left(\frac{2}{3m^*}\right) + \frac{2}{\pi}\sqrt{1-\frac{4}{9(m^*)^2}}, \quad \text{for} \quad m^* \geq \frac{4}{3}.
    \end{equation}
    Hence, for the \hl{six-step limit} one obtains
    \begin{equation}
        \lim_{m^*\to\infty} m^{(1)} = \frac{3}{\pi}\lim_{m^*\to\infty}\left(m^*\arcsin\!\left(\frac{2}{3m^*}\right)\right) + \frac{2}{\pi} = \frac{2}{\pi} + \frac{2}{\pi} = \frac{4}{\pi}.
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Fundamental modulation characteristic %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Achievable fundamental modulation for the min-max injection}
    \begin{figure}
        \centering
        \begin{tikzpicture}
            \begin{axis}[
                    width=0.88\textwidth,
                    height=0.65\textheight,
                    xmin=0,
                    xmax=2.2,
                    ymin=0,
                    ymax=1.6,
                    grid=major,
                    xlabel={$m^*$},
                    ylabel={$m^{(1)}$},
                    xtick={0, 0.5, 1, 2/sqrt(3), 4/3, 2.0},
                    xticklabels={$0$,$\frac{1}{2}$, $1$, $\frac{2}{\sqrt{3}}$, $\frac{4}{3}$, $2$},
                    ytick={0, 0.5, 1, 2/sqrt(3), 4/pi},
                    yticklabels={$0$, $\frac{1}{2}$, $1$,$\nicefrac{2}{\sqrt{3}}$, $\nicefrac{4}{\pi}$},
                    domain=0:2.2,
                    samples=200,
                    clip=false,
                    every axis plot/.append style={thick},
                ]
                \addplot[signalalpha, domain=0:2/sqrt(3)] {x};
                \addplot[signalalpha, domain=2/sqrt(3):4/3] {x - (3*x/pi)*((pi/180)*acos(2/(sqrt(3)*x))) + (2*sqrt(3)/pi)*sqrt(1 - 4/(3*x^2))};
                \addplot[signalalpha, domain=4/3:2.2] {(3*x/pi)*((pi/180)*asin(2/(3*x))) + (2/pi)*sqrt(1 - 4/(9*x^2))};

                \addplot[black, dashed] coordinates {(0,4/pi) (2.2,4/pi)};
                \addplot[black, dashed] coordinates {(2/sqrt(3),0) (2/sqrt(3),4/pi)};
                \addplot[black, dashed] coordinates {(4/3,0) (4/3,4/pi)};

                \node[fill=white, inner sep=4pt, anchor=south] at (axis cs:0.75,0.2) {\scriptsize Linear modulation};
                \node[fill=white, inner sep=4pt, anchor=south] at (axis cs:1.4,0.2) {\scriptsize Overmodulation};
                \draw[{Latex[length=4pt,width=4pt]}-{Latex[length=4pt,width=4pt]}, thick] (axis cs:1.1547,0.5) -- (axis cs:1.3333,0.5);
                \node[fill=white, inner sep=1pt, rotate=90, anchor=west] at (axis cs:1.25,0.55) {\scriptsize Region I};
                \draw[{Latex[length=4pt,width=4pt]}-{Latex[length=4pt,width=4pt]}, thick] (axis cs:1.3333,0.5) -- (axis cs:2.2,0.5);
                \node[fill=white, inner sep=1pt, anchor=south] at (axis cs:1.6667,0.55) {\scriptsize Region II};

                \node[fill=white, inner sep=1pt, anchor=south] at (axis cs:1.75,1.3) {\scriptsize Six-step limit};

            \end{axis}
        \end{tikzpicture}
        \caption{Achievable normalized fundamental modulation amplitude as a function of the reference modulation index for the min-max injection clipping law.}
        \label{fig:min_max_injection_fundamental_modulation_characteristic}
    \end{figure}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Compensating the overmodulation nonlinearity %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Compensating the overmodulation nonlinearity}
    \begin{itemize}
        \item The controller output can be considered a combination of a fundamental voltage amplitude and a voltage angle $\theta$, i.e., $\bm{u} = \bm{u}_{\upalpha\upbeta} = \begin{bmatrix}
                      m^{(1)} \cos(\theta) & m^{(1)} \sin(\theta)
                  \end{bmatrix}^\top$ (neglecting harmonics).
        \item Within the six-step limit, the overmodulation nonlinearity can be (partially) compensated by an inverse modulation gain control.
        \item However, this does not compensate for the voltage angle issue, i.e., the lack of setting the voltage amplitude and angle independently during overmodulation.
    \end{itemize}
    \begin{figure}
        \centering
        \begin{circuitikz}
            \draw (0,0) node[tdcacshape] (conv) {};
            \draw (conv.ac mid out) to [tmultiwire] ++(0.75,0)  to [currtap, name=ct1] ++(0.75,0) to ++(0.25,0) node[threephasemotorshaftshape, anchor = west mid] (motor) {};
            \draw node[ctrlblock, align = center, left = of conv] (mod) {Modulator};
            \draw[->] (mod.east) --  node[midway, above] {$s$} (conv.west);
            \draw node[ctrlblock, align = center, left = of mod] (comp) {$m^*=f^{-1}(m^{(1)})$};
            \draw[->] (comp.east) --  node[midway, above] {$\bm{u}'$} (mod.west);
            \draw node[ctrlblock, align = center, left = of comp] (tctrl) {Torque \\controller};
            \draw[->] (tctrl.east) --  node[midway, above] {$\bm{u}$} (comp.west);
            \draw[-] (ct1.tap) -- ++(0,-1) node[name = A] {};
            \draw[shadecolor] ($(A)!.5!(tctrl.south |- A)$) node[ctrlblock, align = center] (obs) {Observer};
            \draw[->] (ct1.tap) |- (obs.east);
            \draw[->] (obs.west) -| (tctrl.south);
            \draw ($(obs.west)!.5!(obs.west -| tctrl.south)$) node[above] {$x$};
            \draw node[left = of tctrl] (B){};
            \draw[->] (B) -- node[midway, above] {$T^*$} (tctrl.west);
        \end{circuitikz}
        \caption{Compensating the overmodulation nonlinearity by an inverse modulation gain control, i.e., inverting the modulation characteristic $m^{(1)}=f(m^*)$ from \figref{fig:min_max_injection_fundamental_modulation_characteristic}.}
        \label{fig:inverse_modulation_gain_ctrl}
    \end{figure}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\subsection{Discontinous flat-top pulse width modulation}
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Continuous vs. discontinuous PWM %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Continuous vs.\ discontinuous PWM schemes}
    \begin{columns}[onlytextwidth, t]
        \begin{column}{0.49\textwidth}
            \textbf{Continuous PWM}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item All three-phase references are modulated continuously.
                \item Zero-voltage injection is a continuous function of the reference vector, e.g., the min-max injection.
                \item Lower low-order distortion, but higher switching activity.
            \end{itemize}
        \end{column}
        \begin{column}{0.49\textwidth}
            \textbf{Discontinuous PWM}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item The zero-sequence is chosen such that (at least) one phase satisfies
                      \begin{equation}
                          s_p^{**}(t)=\pm 1, \quad p\in\{\mathrm{a,b,c}\},
                      \end{equation}
                      over a finite interval (\hl{clamped leg}).
                \item This reduces switching losses, but changes the harmonic spectrum.
            \end{itemize}
        \end{column}
    \end{columns}
    \begin{block}{Remark}
        Discontinuous PWM (DPWM) schemes offer similar fundamental modulation capability as continuous schemes, but with reduced switching losses at the cost of increased low-order harmonics. There are several DPWM variants which differ in the choice of the clamping angle and the clamped leg with the flat-top modulation, as considered next, being a common scheme.
    \end{block}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Discontinuous flat-top modulation %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Discontinuous flat-top modulation}
    Consider a balanced sinusoidal reference as from \eqref{eq:balanced_sinusoidal_reference_PWM}. Define the phase with the largest absolute instantaneous reference as
    \begin{equation}
        p(\theta)\in \operatorname*{arg\,max}_{i\in\{\mathrm{a,b,c}\}}\left|s_i^*(\theta)\right|.
    \end{equation}
    The \hl{flat-top zero-sequence injection} is then chosen as
    \begin{equation}
        s_0(\theta)=s_{p(\theta)}^*(\theta)-\operatorname{sgn}\!\left(s_{p(\theta)}^*(\theta)\right).
        \label{eq:flat_top_zero_sequence_general}
    \end{equation}
    With
    \begin{equation}
        s^*_{\max}=\max\{s_\mathrm{a}^*,s_\mathrm{b}^*,s_\mathrm{c}^*\}, \qquad
        s^*_{\min}=\min\{s_\mathrm{a}^*,s_\mathrm{b}^*,s_\mathrm{c}^*\},
    \end{equation}
    one may write
    \begin{equation}
        s_0=
        \begin{cases}
            s^*_{\max}-1, & s^*_{\max}\geq -s^*_{\min}, \\
            s^*_{\min}+1, & s^*_{\max}< -s^*_{\min}.
        \end{cases}
        \label{eq:flat_top_zero_sequence_piecewise}
    \end{equation}
    Thus, one phase is clamped to \(+1\) or \(-1\) in each \(60^\circ\) interval, yielding the characteristic \hl{flat-top PWM sequence}.
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% DPWM flat-top example ($m^*=0.5$) %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{DPWM flat-top example ($m^*=0.5$)}
    \begin{figure}
        \begin{tikzpicture}
            \pgfplotsset{table/search path={fig/lec02}}
            \begin{groupplot}[group style={group size=1 by 5, xticklabels at = edge bottom, vertical sep=0.25cm}, height=0.39\textheight, width=0.875\textwidth, xmin=0, xmax=2*pi, grid,clip = false, ymin = -1.1, ymax =1.1, xtick = {0, pi/2, pi, 3/2*pi, 2*pi}, xticklabels = {$0$,$\nicefrac{1}{2}\pi$,$\pi$, $\nicefrac{3}{2}\pi$, $2\pi$}, ytick = {-1, 0, 1}, yticklabels = {$-1$, $0$, $1$}]

                % Top plot: original normalized voltage references
                \nextgroupplot[ylabel = {$s_i^*(t)$}, ymin = -1.1, ymax =1.1]
                \addplot[signalalpha, thick] table[x=wt, y=d_a, col sep=comma] {PWM_three-phase_flat-top_mod05_example.csv};
                \addplot[signalbeta, thick] table[x=wt, y=d_b, col sep=comma] {PWM_three-phase_flat-top_mod05_example.csv};
                \addplot[signalgamma, thick] table[x=wt, y=d_c, col sep=comma] {PWM_three-phase_flat-top_mod05_example.csv};
                \node[signalalpha, anchor=north, fill = white, inner sep = 1pt] at (axis cs: pi/2, 0.95) {\small $s_\mathrm{a}^*$};
                \node[signalbeta, anchor=north, fill = white, inner sep = 1pt] at (axis cs: 7*pi/6, 0.95) {\small $s_\mathrm{b}^*$};
                \node[signalgamma, anchor=north, fill = white, inner sep = 1pt] at (axis cs: 11*pi/6, 0.95) {\small $s_\mathrm{c}^*$};

                % middle plot: injected duty cycles and carrier
                \nextgroupplot[ylabel = {$s_i^{**}(t), c(t)$}, ymin = -1.25, ymax =1.25]

                \addplot[signalbeta, dashed, thick] table[x=wt, y=d_b_mod, col sep=comma] {PWM_three-phase_flat-top_mod05_example.csv};
                \addplot[signalgamma, dashed, thick] table[x=wt, y=d_c_mod, col sep=comma] {PWM_three-phase_flat-top_mod05_example.csv};
                \addplot[signalalpha, thick] table[x=wt, y=d_a_mod_clip, col sep=comma] {PWM_three-phase_flat-top_mod05_example.csv};
                \addplot[signalbeta, thick] table[x=wt, y=d_b_mod_clip, col sep=comma] {PWM_three-phase_flat-top_mod05_example.csv};
                \addplot[signalgamma, thick] table[x=wt, y=d_c_mod_clip, col sep=comma] {PWM_three-phase_flat-top_mod05_example.csv};
                \addplot[black, thick] table[x=wt, y=c, col sep=comma] {PWM_three-phase_flat-top_mod05_example.csv};
                \node[signalalpha, anchor=north, fill = white, inner sep = 0.1pt] at (axis cs: pi/2, 0.70) {\small $s_\mathrm{a}^{**}$};
                \node[signalbeta, anchor=north, fill = white, inner sep = 0.1pt] at (axis cs: 6.6*pi/6, 0.7) {\small $s_\mathrm{b}^{**}$};
                \node[signalgamma, anchor=north, fill = white, inner sep = 0.1pt] at (axis cs: 11.4*pi/6, 0.7) {\small $s_\mathrm{c}^{**}$};
                \node[black, anchor=center] at (axis cs: 0.3, -0.4) {\small $c$};

                % switching sequence phase a
                \nextgroupplot[ylabel = {$s_\mathrm{a}(t)$}, height=0.26\textheight, ytick={-1,1}, yticklabels={$-1$,$+1$}, ymin = -1.25, ymax =1.25]
                \addplot[signalalpha, thick] table[x=wt, y=sa, col sep=comma] {PWM_three-phase_flat-top_mod05_example.csv};

                % switching sequence phase b
                \nextgroupplot[ylabel = {$s_\mathrm{b}(t)$}, height=0.26\textheight, ytick={-1,1}, yticklabels={$-1$,$+1$}, ymin = -1.25, ymax =1.25]

                % switching sequence phase c
                \nextgroupplot[ylabel = {$s_\mathrm{c}(t)$}, xlabel={$\omega t$}, xlabel style={yshift=1ex}, height=0.26\textheight, ytick={-1,1}, yticklabels={$-1$,$+1$}, ymin = -1.25, ymax =1.25]
                \addplot[signalgamma, thick] table[x=wt, y=sc, col sep=comma] {PWM_three-phase_flat-top_mod05_example.csv};
            \end{groupplot}
        \end{tikzpicture}
    \end{figure}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% DPWM flat-top example ($m^*=1$) %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{DPWM flat-top example ($m^*=1$)}
    \begin{figure}
        \begin{tikzpicture}
            \pgfplotsset{table/search path={fig/lec02}}
            \begin{groupplot}[group style={group size=1 by 5, xticklabels at = edge bottom, vertical sep=0.25cm}, height=0.39\textheight, width=0.875\textwidth, xmin=0, xmax=2*pi, grid,clip = false, ymin = -1.1, ymax =1.1, xtick = {0, pi/2, pi, 3/2*pi, 2*pi}, xticklabels = {$0$,$\nicefrac{1}{2}\pi$,$\pi$, $\nicefrac{3}{2}\pi$, $2\pi$}, ytick = {-1, 0, 1}, yticklabels = {$-1$, $0$, $1$}]

                % Top plot: original normalized voltage references
                \nextgroupplot[ylabel = {$s_i^*(t)$}, ymin = -1.1, ymax =1.1]

                \addplot[signalgamma, thick] table[x=wt, y=d_c, col sep=comma] {PWM_three-phase_flat-top_mod1_example.csv};

                % switching sequence phase a
                \nextgroupplot[ylabel = {$s_\mathrm{a}(t)$}, height=0.26\textheight, ytick={-1,1}, yticklabels={$-1$,$+1$}, ymin = -1.25, ymax =1.25]
                \addplot[signalalpha, thick] table[x=wt, y=sa, col sep=comma] {PWM_three-phase_flat-top_mod1_example.csv};

                % switching sequence phase b
                \nextgroupplot[ylabel = {$s_\mathrm{b}(t)$}, height=0.26\textheight, ytick={-1,1}, yticklabels={$-1$,$+1$}, ymin = -1.25, ymax =1.25]
                \addplot[signalbeta, thick] table[x=wt, y=sb, col sep=comma] {PWM_three-phase_flat-top_mod1_example.csv};

                \nextgroupplot[ylabel = {$s_\mathrm{c}(t)$}, xlabel={$\omega t$}, xlabel style={yshift=1ex}, height=0.26\textheight, ytick={-1,1}, yticklabels={$-1$,$+1$}, ymin = -1.25, ymax =1.25]

\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Flat-top voltage capacity %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Voltage capacity of the flat-top injection}
    Using the first-sector parametrization from \eqref{eq:first_sector_hexagon_lin_comb_abc},
    \begin{equation*}
        \bm{s}^*_\mathrm{abc} =
        \begin{bmatrix}
            \nicefrac{4}{3}\tau_1 + \nicefrac{2}{3}\tau_2  &
            -\nicefrac{2}{3}\tau_1 + \nicefrac{2}{3}\tau_2 &
            -\nicefrac{2}{3}\tau_1 - \nicefrac{4}{3}\tau_2
        \end{bmatrix}^\top,
        \qquad
        \tau_1,\tau_2\geq 0, \quad \tau_1+\tau_2\leq 1,
    \end{equation*}
    the \hl{flat-top PWM definition} clamps the leading positive phase to the upper rail for $\theta\in[-\nicefrac{\pi}{6}, \nicefrac{\pi}{6}]$. Hence, within the upper first sector part, phase \(\mathrm{a}\) is clamped, yielding
    \begin{equation}
        s_0=s_\mathrm{a}^*-1
        \qquad \Rightarrow \qquad
        s_\mathrm{a}^{**}=s_\mathrm{a}^*-s_0=1.
        \label{eq:flat_top_clamping_phase_a}
    \end{equation}
    Consequently, only the modulated phases \(\mathrm{b}\) and \(\mathrm{c}\) must be checked. Inserting \eqref{eq:flat_top_clamping_phase_a} into \eqref{eq:first_sector_hexagon_lin_comb_abc} gives
    \begin{equation}
        s_\mathrm{b}^{**}=1-2\tau_1, \qquad
        s_\mathrm{c}^{**}=1-2(\tau_1+\tau_2).
    \end{equation}
    Because \(0\leq \tau_1\leq 1\) and \(0\leq \tau_1+\tau_2\leq 1\), it follows directly that
    \begin{equation}
        -1\leq s_\mathrm{b}^{**}\leq 1, \qquad -1\leq s_\mathrm{c}^{**}\leq 1.
    \end{equation}
    Thus, every reference in the \hl{first upper sector part of the hexagon} is realizable with flat-top PWM: phase \(\mathrm{a}\) is fixed at \(+1\), while phases \(\mathrm{b}\) and \(\mathrm{c}\) remain within the admissible interval. By symmetry, the \hl{entire voltage hexagon}, including its corners, can be reached.
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Flat-top linear modulation range %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Flat-top linear modulation range}
    In the positive \(\mathrm{a}\)-clamp sector $-\nicefrac{\pi}{6}\leq \theta \leq \nicefrac{\pi}{6}$,  one has \(s_0(\theta)=s_\mathrm{a}^*(\theta)-1\), yielding
    \begin{equation}
        s_\mathrm{a}^{**}(\theta)=1,
        \qquad
        s_\mathrm{b}^{**}(\theta)=1-\sqrt{3}m^*\cos\!\left(\theta+\frac{\pi}{6}\right),
        \qquad
        s_\mathrm{c}^{**}(\theta)=1-\sqrt{3}m^*\cos\!\left(\theta-\frac{\pi}{6}\right).
        \label{eq:flat_top_positive_a_sector}
    \end{equation}
    Since
    \begin{equation}
        \cos\!\left(\theta\pm\frac{\pi}{6}\right)\in\left[\frac{1}{2},1\right]
        \qquad \forall\, \theta\in\left[-\frac{\pi}{6},\frac{\pi}{6}\right],
    \end{equation}
    the following must hold to prevent clipping of a further phase:
    \begin{equation}
        1-\sqrt{3}m^*
        \leq
        s_\mathrm{b}^{**}(\theta),\, s_\mathrm{c}^{**}(\theta)
        \leq
        1-\frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}m^*.
    \end{equation}
    Therefore, requiring the non-clamped phases to stay within the \hl{linear modulation} range yields
    \begin{equation}
        1-\sqrt{3}m^* \geq -1
        \qquad \Leftrightarrow \qquad
        m^*\leq \frac{2}{\sqrt{3}}.
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Flat-top overmodulation regions %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Flat-top overmodulation regions}
    For the flat-top overmodulation range define
    \begin{equation}
        \gamma=\arccos\!\left(\frac{2}{\sqrt{3}m^*}\right),
        \qquad
        \frac{2}{\sqrt{3}}<m^*\leq \frac{4}{\sqrt{3}}.
        \label{eq:flat_top_gamma_definition}
    \end{equation}
    With \eqref{eq:flat_top_gamma_definition} and \eqref{eq:flat_top_positive_a_sector}, on the positive half-sector \(0\leq \theta\leq \nicefrac{\pi}{6}\), phase \(\mathrm{c}\) is clipped for
    \begin{equation}
        \theta\in\left[\frac{\pi}{6}-\gamma,\frac{\pi}{6}\right].
        \label{eq:region_I_flat_top_theta}
    \end{equation}
    If \(\gamma>\nicefrac{\pi}{6}\), then additionally phase \(\mathrm{b}\) is clipped for
    \begin{equation}
        \theta\in\left[0,\gamma-\frac{\pi}{6}\right].
        \label{eq:region_II_flat_top_theta}
    \end{equation}
    Hence, from inserting \eqref{eq:flat_top_gamma_definition} in \eqref{eq:region_I_flat_top_theta} and \eqref{eq:region_II_flat_top_theta}, the flat-top overmodulation splits into
    \begin{itemize}
        \item \textbf{Region I:} \(\nicefrac{2}{\sqrt{3}}<m^*\leq \nicefrac{4}{3}\),
        \item \textbf{Region II:} \(m^*>  \nicefrac{4}{3}\).
    \end{itemize}
\end{frame}
